<script>
  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_9c133261-f215-4fb4-a34b-9df3cbe5dc0e'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };
    if (typeof AppleID !== "undefined") {
      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();
    }

<span id="freeTextContainer3345488642798624357">A HEART TORMENTED <br/><br/>Erienne's father had given her hand to the richest suitor. She was now Lady Saxton, mistress of a great manor all but ruined by fire, wife to a man whose mysteriously shrouded form aroused fear and pity. Yet even as she fell in love with her adoring husband, Erienne despaired of freeing her heart from the dashingly handsome Yankee who couldn't forget her.</span>
  <span id="freeText3345488642798624357" style="display:none">A HEART TORMENTED <br /><br />Erienne's father had given her hand to the richest suitor. She was now Lady Saxton, mistress of a great manor all but ruined by fire, wife to a man whose mysteriously shrouded form aroused fear and pity. Yet even as she fell in love with her adoring husband, Erienne despaired of freeing her heart from the dashingly handsome Yankee who couldn't forget her. The beautiful Erienne, once filled with young dreams of romance, was now a wife and woman ... torn between the two men she loved.</span>

<div id="review_595127984" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/595127984" />
    <a title="Allarice" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7899234-allarice"><img alt="Allarice" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1377805816p2/7899234.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/595127984?book_show_action=true">Apr 19, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Allarice" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Allarice" href="/user/show/7899234-allarice">Allarice</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer595127984" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11713997102634230749">So. <b>This book...confounds me.</b><br/><br/>I wanted to like it so badly. It started off so well. Or, rather, the plot sounded so good to begin with. A collection of my favorite romance tropes: Beauty and the Beast AND a married couple AND rooting for the underdog. <br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380418098ra/827602.gif' width='400' height='auto' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>When a audience is <i>this</i> eager to like a novel, <u>what are the chances the book could possibly go wrong</u>?<br/><br/><br/><br/><b>1. Nice to Meet You, Miss; I'm Gary Stu.</b><br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380418325ra/828231.gif' width='400' height='auto' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><i>"Her mind had begun to race, forming thoughts totally counter to what they had been earlier. <b>The man was nea</b></i></span>
  <span id="freeText11713997102634230749" style="display:none">So. <b>This book...confounds me.</b><br><br>I wanted to like it so badly. It started off so well. Or, rather, the plot sounded so good to begin with. A collection of my favorite romance tropes: Beauty and the Beast AND a married couple AND rooting for the underdog. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380418098ra/827602.gif" width="400" height="auto" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>When a audience is <i>this</i> eager to like a novel, <u>what are the chances the book could possibly go wrong</u>?<br><br><br><br><b>1. Nice to Meet You, Miss; I'm Gary Stu.</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380418325ra/828231.gif" width="400" height="auto" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><i>"Her mind had begun to race, forming thoughts totally counter to what they had been earlier. <b>The man was nearly perfect! Without visible flaw!</b> Yet the question persisted. If the man was willing to wed, how could he reach a mature age without being entrapped by at least a dozen women? <b>There must be a flaw! her common sense raged. Knowing Father, there is a flaw!</b>"</i> - <i>A Rose in Winter</i><br><br>...There isn't. Throughout the entire novel, there is not a <b>single flaw</b> in the hero. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Especially in terms of looks. Rather defeats the purpose of the "beast" part. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> <br><br>See, I understand there is quite a flow of Gary Stus and Mary Sues in romances. However, <i>A Rose in Winter</i> takes this to the EXTREME. These people aren't people. They are caricatures of people. <br><br>Seriously. When the heroine does nothing but rail about the perfection of the hero based on his looks, and the hero has no hobbies (other than perhaps <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[inexplicably dressing up like the Phantom of the Opera minus the panache factor <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>), no weaknesses, no quirks, NOTHING throughout the entire freaking novel, well...unfortunately, the hero is left as flat as Flat Finn. (And the heroine is no better, but we'll get there.)<br><br><br><br><b>2. As his small boat scudded before a brisk breeze under a sapphire sky dappled with cerulean clouds with indigo bases, through cobalt seas that deepened to navy nearer the boat and faded to azure at the horizon, Ian was at a loss as to why he felt blue.</b><br><br><i>"<b>How deeply has this wench entrapped me?</b>" he mused. "<b>She has snared my spirit and my soul. Like a hawk, she has snatched them in full flight.</b>" He shook his head. "<b>But unlike the wild bird, she harmed them not. Nay, rather took them to her breast and breathed new life into them, and they have been so blissfully refreshed, my heart is nigh to bursting. Before I came to these shores, I would have sworn my ships would ever be my love, for no maid had so captivated me as the thrill of skimming the seas beneath billowing sails.</b>"</i> - <i>A Rose in Winter</i><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380418325ra/828232.gif" width="400" height="auto" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>It's not that I dislike dense prose. I can deal with description; Meredith Duran's <i>Duke of Shadows</i> is one of my favorite romances of all time. Sherry Thomas tugs on my heartstrings almost every book. Departing from Romancelandia, some of my favorite novels are <i>A Tale of Two Cities</i> and the <i>Count of Monte Cristo.</i><br><br>...But when description is used without the slightest thought for occasion, thesauruses become the new human brain, the act of making pancakes is sensationalized to a life and death experience, metaphors are utterly abused, and each tree in a forest is given an individual sentence of description - whether likening it to dark and gloomy skeletons or imposing statues - I draw the line. <br><br>Basically, it's a <s>tragedy</s> <u>miracle</u> I made it through the book. <br><br><br><br><b>3. Brain Capacity of Heroine.</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380418325ra/828233.gif" width="400" height="auto" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I actually do not believe I have met a whinier, more vapid, uninteresting heroine. Erienne is shallow as hell. She ranks every one of her suitors on looks - in fact, it is Christopher who enlightens her of their characters <i>after</i> she has dismissed them. She despises her husband, who has been nothing but kind to her, for about five hundred pages for no reason except that he's scarred. Is it reasonable to be not-attracted to a scarred man? Yes. Is it reasonable to treat him like a monster, call him the 'embodiment of [her] worst nightmares,' and act as if touching his sleeve is utterly disgusting, even when he a)treats her like an equal b)is considerate of all her feelings and c)basically grants her every whim? No. She is also <s>stupid</s> not very smart; she rides through the street in broad daylight to "escape" from her father (who can totally see her...), cannot solve the most obvious conundrum in the world, and acts like a silly little girl: she literally stomps her feet, tosses her hair, and kicks the hero in the shin. She is also completely powerless in the story and requires a big strong man to save her from <i>everything</i>.<br><br>In summary, Erienne is a faux-feisty gorgeous beauty (think the face that launched a thousand ships, or at least, ten thousand pounds) with the depth of a puddle and the brain of a poodle. It would be nice if the Beauty had something to recommend her other than her, you know, <i>beauty</i>.<br><br><br><br><b>4. The Plot</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380418325ra/828234.gif" width="400" height="auto" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>First: immensely predictable. Not that that's bad, necessarily - I know romances are generally guaranteed a HEA - but really, when the entire conflict (because <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[the thing with the Saxon family does not deserve the characterization of "conflict" <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>) hinges on the heroine being tempted between two men, it's minorly frustrating when you figure out the big secret within the first fifty pages. <br><br>Second: the hero's explanation for why he does what he does is stupid. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[The way I read the wedding scene, both the barrister AND Erienne's father were merely witnesses. That means his consent is not necessary. Which then means that Christopher could have said a few nice words instead of being all macho-insulting and eloped with her. I get he thought she hated him, but seriously, you think she'd hate a man who tricked her into marrying him any less? Why did he think pretending to be a crippled 'monster' would help his case? And even if it was absolutely necessary for him to marry her under the guise of "Lord Saxton," why not send a proxy (which was common practice those days) rather than going to all the trouble of that stupid scheme (aka dressing up as Darth Vader)? <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>Third: I still don't understand Erienne's fascination with Christopher. Saxon is kind to her, yes. Is Christopher? Not really. And, yet, before she connects the two personalities, she's swooning over Christopher. I found their "love" more of:<br><br>Chris: Holy cow, what a babe!<br>Eri: Golly, he's smokin'!<br><br>...I didn't buy it. <br><br>Fourth: The 'mystery' and the 'grand reveal.' Especially the night rider. Enough said.<br><br><br><br><b>Basically, this book made me want to chuck it at a wall multiple times. Plot, characterization, writing style were all crazy annoying. It destroyed a scheme that I thought would be a sure success given what I like to read. <br><br>But, STILL, for whatever reason, I finished the book.<br><br>And because somehow, this book did manage to grip me enough that I slugged through it (reading at a quarter of the pace I usually do), I awarded it an extra star for a grand total of TWO STARS.</b><br></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="11713997102634230749" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2761423388" />
    <a title="Stacey is Sassy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/12062194-stacey-is-sassy"><img alt="Stacey is Sassy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1474185067p2/12062194.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2761423388?book_show_action=true">Mar 31, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Stacey is Sassy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Stacey is Sassy" href="/user/show/12062194-stacey-is-sassy">Stacey is Sassy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/6093617-a-rose-in-winter">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12062194-stacey-is-sassy?shelf=historical-romance">historical-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12062194-stacey-is-sassy?shelf=intrigue">intrigue</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12062194-stacey-is-sassy?shelf=douchewaffles-galore">douchewaffles-galore</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12062194-stacey-is-sassy?shelf=angry-fix">angry-fix</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12062194-stacey-is-sassy?shelf=cranky-hero">cranky-hero</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12062194-stacey-is-sassy?shelf=the-good-guy-hero">the-good-guy-hero</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12062194-stacey-is-sassy?shelf=if-this-guy-was-real">if-this-guy-was-real</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2761423388" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5929435530996762282"><b>I'm out of practice...</b><br/><br/>I really enjoyed my step back in time reading <i>A Rose in Winter</i> but it also brought back a horrific memory. I have loved historical romances for many years and would save up every dollar I had to buy more. I look back at that time with fondness and even wish I could get back to that time where life didn't have as many interruptions. The horrific part of that memory...I gave away all my paperback's when I got married. I mistakenly thought *I have the love of my life in front </span>
  <span id="freeText5929435530996762282" style="display:none"><b>I'm out of practice...</b><br><br>I really enjoyed my step back in time reading <i>A Rose in Winter</i> but it also brought back a horrific memory. I have loved historical romances for many years and would save up every dollar I had to buy more. I look back at that time with fondness and even wish I could get back to that time where life didn't have as many interruptions. The horrific part of that memory...I gave away all my paperback's when I got married. I mistakenly thought *I have the love of my life in front of me, I don't need to read romance any more.* Yes, I'm a bloody idiot!<br><br>I made the mistake of sneaking a peek at a spoiler before I started <i>A Rose in Winter.</i><br><br><b><i><u>DON'T DO IT!!!</u></i></b><br><br>Do not look at spoilers as it will ruin your whole experience. You don't need it. Sure, you might suffer a little anxiety but if you really put your mind to it, I'm sure you'll work out the mystery in good time.<br><br>This was a great story but it was LOOOOONG!! I'm out of practice reading these long and overly descriptive stories. I think I've become impatient and looking for the quick fix instead of sitting back and enjoying the ride. I need to be more relaxed about my reading experiences and appreciate the effort and skill the authors show when they set their scenes.<br><br>Erienne was a heroine I came to admire. At times I was frustrated with her shallow beliefs but then again she was surrounded by people who looked at her and only saw a pretty face. I would have loved to step in a few times and hand out a lecture or two. Her father was one of the most horrid characters I've ever met and he never learnt from his mistakes.<br><br>If I could only step back in time...I would NOT donate my beautiful paperbacks AND I would NOT look at the spoiler for this one.<br><br>If you enjoy a good historical romance with plenty of grit and a lot of accuracies (or what I think of as accurate) portraying the hardships of women at that time, I highly recommend <i>A Rose in Winter.</i> I will definitely be reading more from this author in the future.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1548709401i/26982519.jpg" width="300" height="300" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="5929435530996762282" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="maricar" class="user" itemprop="url" name="maricar" href="/user/show/750368-maricar">maricar</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/750368-maricar?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/750368-maricar?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer11847538" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer790391630126798482">I loved how ms. woodiwiss portrayed Lord Saxton--fierce on the outside but oh-so-tender when with Erienne. personally, the way he was described, i did not feel he was that hideous. i actually preferred him over Christopher. before any revelations were finally made open, i found myself hotly rooting for Lord Saxton. for me, Christopher (allegedly removed from Lord Saxton's presence) was cocky and outrageous. handsome as the devil of course, and totally overwhelming. but somehow he didnt quite mea</span>
  <span id="freeText790391630126798482" style="display:none">I loved how ms. woodiwiss portrayed Lord Saxton--fierce on the outside but oh-so-tender when with Erienne. personally, the way he was described, i did not feel he was that hideous. i actually preferred him over Christopher. before any revelations were finally made open, i found myself hotly rooting for Lord Saxton. for me, Christopher (allegedly removed from Lord Saxton's presence) was cocky and outrageous. handsome as the devil of course, and totally overwhelming. but somehow he didnt quite measure up to the dark and brooding presence and, may i say, charisma, of Lord Saxton. <br /><br />so it was simply a most delightful surprise when Erienne was shown the truth. i loved what transpired then between her and her husband. however, i did not quite find myself favoring Erienne. her maidenly qualms in the presence of Lord Saxton were simply way exaggerated---there were times i wanted to shake her silly for harboring overblown images about her husband. <br /><br />All-in-all, A Rose in Winter is a wonderful story. as is usual for ms. woodiwiss, her dialogues for her characters were quite effusive, but still, for a story with a fairy-like quality such as this, the rich interplay of words was appropriate. when one stumbles upon the tender scenes, the dialogue is instrumental in evoking wistful fantasies of what it would be like to belong to someone like the hero of the story. </span>
  <a data-text-id="790391630126798482" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_112347228" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/112347228" />
    <a title="Vivian" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3947172-vivian"><img alt="Vivian" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1458107851p2/3947172.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/112347228?book_show_action=true">Jul 19, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Vivian" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Vivian" href="/user/show/3947172-vivian">Vivian</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3947172-vivian?shelf=romance-hist">romance-hist</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer112347228" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8627608453313730788"><> Reread in July 2018 <><br/><br/>Fast paced story of Erienne Fleming, impoverished daughter of Mawbry's mayor. She bears a resemblance to Catherine from Taming of the Shrew at the start, but very quickly it becomes obvious with the cards she's been dealt in life that it really isn't surprising. <br/><br/>Swords, fire, murder, mayhem, auctioned female, Georgian extravagance and true love. *sigh* Good stuff.<br/><br/><b>
  <blockquote> I have found my rose in winter. You are my own precious love, promised to me evermore.</blockquote>
</b><br/><br/>Woodiwiss had a go</span>
  <span id="freeText8627608453313730788" style="display:none">&lt;&gt; Reread in July 2018 &lt;&gt;<br /><br />Fast paced story of Erienne Fleming, impoverished daughter of Mawbry's mayor. She bears a resemblance to Catherine from Taming of the Shrew at the start, but very quickly it becomes obvious with the cards she's been dealt in life that it really isn't surprising. <br /><br />Swords, fire, murder, mayhem, auctioned female, Georgian extravagance and true love. *sigh* Good stuff.<br /><br /><b>
  <blockquote> I have found my rose in winter. You are my own precious love, promised to me evermore.</blockquote>
</b><br /><br />Woodiwiss had a good command of language and used it very well. The descriptives are lovely and the sentiment, passionate to treacle sweet. <br /><br /><blockquote>
  <b>"Honor you?" he breathed. "Sweetest Erienne, how could I not? You are ever in my thoughts bending me, twisting me, plucking at the fibers of my mind. The man inside me trembles whenever you're near, and I groan in agony for the touch of your hand laid upon me in a soft caress. I am beset with desire for you, and if I thought for one moment that you would not loathe me forever, I would ease my lusts this very night, be you willing or nay."</b>
</blockquote><br /><br />Just as wonderful as I remember. Liberal use of the term Yankee in this KEW story, but instead of Gray v. Blue as in my last one, this is England v. newly-minted America. Probably my favorite Woodiwiss novel, though I am planning to reread The Wolf and the Dove later this year with Andrea, so it could be a toss up. </span>
  <a data-text-id="8627608453313730788" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">
          

<tr class="no_border feedFooterReview" id="update_comment_stuff_Review112347228">
  <td colspan="2">

<div id="review_358640745" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/358640745" />
    <a title="Regan Walker" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7363897-regan-walker"><img alt="Regan Walker" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442636914p2/7363897.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/358640745?book_show_action=true">Jun 30, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Regan Walker" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Regan Walker" href="/user/show/7363897-regan-walker">Regan Walker</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/6093617-a-rose-in-winter">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7363897-regan-walker?shelf=5-star-reads">5-star-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7363897-regan-walker?shelf=favorite-keepers">favorite-keepers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7363897-regan-walker?shelf=18th-century">18th-century</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7363897-regan-walker?shelf=favorite-hero">favorite-hero</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer358640745" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16920195852874641921">A Choice Between Love and Honor in a Great Georgian Romance!<br/><br/>Kathleen Woodiwiss has written some truly great romances. She was a great storyteller. This one at well over 500 pages is no exception. A rose in winter...a flower blooming out of time...a sign of true love to come. Ah yes...how we love it.<br/><br/>Set in late 18th century England, this is the story of the Sexton noble family, whose lord and his eldest son were killed for their wealth and lands. Now the young lord, who succeeded his father, has </span>
  <span id="freeText16920195852874641921" style="display:none">A Choice Between Love and Honor in a Great Georgian Romance!<br /><br />Kathleen Woodiwiss has written some truly great romances. She was a great storyteller. This one at well over 500 pages is no exception. A rose in winter...a flower blooming out of time...a sign of true love to come. Ah yes...how we love it.<br /><br />Set in late 18th century England, this is the story of the Sexton noble family, whose lord and his eldest son were killed for their wealth and lands. Now the young lord, who succeeded his father, has supposedly died in a fire purposely set to end his life, the same fire that burned a wing of their mansion. <br /><br />Years later, a wealthy Yankee merchant seaman, Christopher Seton, has come to the village of Mawbry seeking a place to live while he settles a debt owed him. He makes inquiries about the old Saxton Hall, still vacant after the death of the young lord. <br /><br />Living in the same village is Erienne, a beauty whose only value to her father (the Mayor) is to be sold to the highest bidder among her many suitors. Her father needs the money to pay his debts, including the one he owes to Seton, who has taken a fancy to Erienne.<br /><br />At the sale, the highest bidder is an agent for a mysterious "Lord Saxton," supposedly the very same lord who was thought burned in the fire. He wears a mask to hide his deformed face and walks with a deep limp. Now wed to the man, Erienne initially fears him, but he is kind and generous to her. She holds him at bay as to their physical relationship. Slowly, she comes to respect and care for him, but alongside this growing feeling for her husband is a growing attraction to the Yankee Seton.<br /><br />Woodiwiss deals us a fast moving hand as the players hide their true motives and their true characters from each other. As we follow along, we are not disappointed. Like her other romances, she weaves a complex tale and provides a rich tapestry of characters. Her descriptions will put you in the scene and leave you wanting more.<br /><br />If you're a Woodiwiss fan, you'll love this one.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="16920195852874641921" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer1008659859" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10647518754094781029">I haven't read this book in years and years, but I still love it. I was just recently looking through my favorite authors I haven't read in years and I just realized that Kathleen E. Woodiwiss died back in 2007. I hadn't heard anything about that and it makes me sad that such a wonderful author had died. This was the first book I ever read of Ms. Woodiwiss and reading it again brings back a sense of deja vu of being wrapped in a warm blanket and reading this wonderful story of the love triangle </span>
  <span id="freeText10647518754094781029" style="display:none">I haven't read this book in years and years, but I still love it. I was just recently looking through my favorite authors I haven't read in years and I just realized that Kathleen E. Woodiwiss died back in 2007. I hadn't heard anything about that and it makes me sad that such a wonderful author had died. This was the first book I ever read of Ms. Woodiwiss and reading it again brings back a sense of deja vu of being wrapped in a warm blanket and reading this wonderful story of the love triangle of Erienne, Christoper Seton and Lord Saxton. I remember thinking years ago (I think I was like in junior high when I read this book for the first time) that it reminded me of Beauty and the Beast. <br><br>Somewhere I have a the paperback version with this cover <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/896625.A_Rose_in_Winter" title="A Rose in Winter by Kathleen E. Woodiwiss" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/books/1327110426s/896625.jpg" alt="A Rose in Winter by Kathleen E. Woodiwiss" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a>. I'd always thought that this was a gorgeous cover and it reminded me of a Michelangelo painting. The cover was what made me read the book. I'm a little sad that the cover isn't on my Kindle version, but I'm at least happy that Ms. Woodiwiss's books are on Kindle. I wish that Judith McNaught's publishers would put her books on Kindle.</span>

<div id="review_344274338" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/344274338" />
    <a title="Christy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2061204-christy"><img alt="Christy" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/344274338?book_show_action=true">Jun 07, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Christy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Christy" href="/user/show/2061204-christy">Christy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">absolutely no one</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2061204-christy?shelf=romance-meetup">romance-meetup</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2061204-christy?shelf=1-own-it-book">1-own-it-book</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2061204-christy?shelf=jeannie-s">jeannie-s</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer344274338" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2814822388105074456">1.5 stars<br/><br/>Oh my, was this book awful. The writing is laughably bad. I love lush, descriptive prose (Sherry Thomas, Loretta Chase). I even love unnecessarily detailed descriptions (Diana Gabaldon). But I just could not stomach the overwrought, purple prose of this book. Here is an example. I defy anyone to read this without gagging:<br/><br/><blockquote>"How deeply has this wench entrapped me?" he mused. "She has snared my spirit and my soul. Like a hawk, she has snatched them in full flight." He shook his head. "But u</blockquote></span>
  <span id="freeText2814822388105074456" style="display:none">1.5 stars<br /><br />Oh my, was this book awful. The writing is laughably bad. I love lush, descriptive prose (Sherry Thomas, Loretta Chase). I even love unnecessarily detailed descriptions (Diana Gabaldon). But I just could not stomach the overwrought, purple prose of this book. Here is an example. I defy anyone to read this without gagging:<br /><br /><blockquote>"How deeply has this wench entrapped me?" he mused. "She has snared my spirit and my soul. Like a hawk, she has snatched them in full flight." He shook his head. "But unlike the wild bird, she harmed them not. Nay, rather took them to her breast and breathed new life into them, and they have been so blissfully refreshed, my heart is nigh to bursting...." </blockquote><br /><br />It goes on but I will spare you. Mind you, he's speaking to himself in an empty room. Hamlet, he's not.<br /><br />And then there is the heroine. I have rarely hated a character as much as I hated Erienne, with her head tossing and foot stamping and general uselessness. At one point she decides to steal a horse and run away from home, so naturally she rides it down the main street where her father can see her fleeing. Why would I want to waste my time on a heroine so stupid? Her abject terror of Lord Saxton because he was scarred was insulting. I was ready for him to throw her back to her other sniveling suitors, and good riddance.<br /><br />Lord Saxton himself was described as a Georgian era Darth Vader, which I found mildly amusing. As the original book was published fairly soon after The Empire Strikes Back came out, I doubt it was coincidental. <br /><br />I actually increased my rating from 1 star to 1.5 stars because there was the glimmer of an interesting plot hidden beneath the layers of horrible writing and ridiculous characterizations. I had the plot figured out by around page 70, but predictability isn't necessarily a fatal flaw in a romance. Beauty and the Beast is one of my favorite tropes, but in most versions, Beauty has something more going for her than her appearance. In this book, she really doesn't, at least for the first half of the book. She does eventually show some degree of loyalty to Lord Saxton, which was her only redeeming virtue and probably the reason I didn't just give up on the book altogether. Well, that and the fact I was reading this for a book club. If I'd been reading it on my own, I would have given up in the first chapter. It's really that bad.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2814822388105074456" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown" >
    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_81465235" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/81465235" />
    <a title="Erin *Proud Book Hoarder*" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3048260-erin-proud-book-hoarder"><img alt="Erin *Proud Book Hoarder*" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1572373103p2/3048260.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/81465235?book_show_action=true">Dec 19, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Erin *Proud Book Hoarder*" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Erin *Proud Book Hoarder*" href="/user/show/3048260-erin-proud-book-hoarder">Erin *Proud Book Hoarder*</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/6093617-a-rose-in-winter">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3048260-erin-proud-book-hoarder?shelf=4-star">4-star</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3048260-erin-proud-book-hoarder?shelf=romance-historical-honeys">romance-historical-honeys</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3048260-erin-proud-book-hoarder?shelf=a-own-book-form">a-own-book-form</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3048260-erin-proud-book-hoarder?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3048260-erin-proud-book-hoarder?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer81465235" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3709428654892201122">With the passing of legendary Kathleen E. Woodiwiss, I wanted to give her books a try. I remember reading something by her as a wee one, but for the life of me can't recall what it was. Browsing online, a friend and I were intrigued to discover the synopsis boasted a scarred, tragic figure as the possible hero. Swooning over the though of a Phantom-of-the-opera type hunk, I quickly nabbed this baby up at the local bookstore during our usual Tuesday night outing, and then sped through the book I </span>
  <span id="freeText3709428654892201122" style="display:none">With the passing of legendary Kathleen E. Woodiwiss, I wanted to give her books a try. I remember reading something by her as a wee one, but for the life of me can't recall what it was. Browsing online, a friend and I were intrigued to discover the synopsis boasted a scarred, tragic figure as the possible hero. Swooning over the though of a Phantom-of-the-opera type hunk, I quickly nabbed this baby up at the local bookstore during our usual Tuesday night outing, and then sped through the book I was reading to start this one.<br /><br />Plot-wise, it's refreshing. A young, maltreated woman has been kept under the bristled thumb of her drunk, nescient father and irresponsibly daft brother. Deep in debt to the man who shot his son during a card-cheating war, the father decides to use his daughter to settle the deal. He refuses to wed her to his enemy, but has no problem putting her up for a hideous auction.<br /><br />Terrified and grief-stricken, Erienne sadly accepts her fate, only to find her new husband-to-be is a scarred figure who covers his face with a menacing, black mask. Terrified of the wealthy figure who slightly resembles a BDSM enthusiast, she cannot master the courage to be his wife in all ways, but slowly finds herself falling for his sweet, caring manner. It's hard to accept her significant other completely, however, when in the back of her mind there's always the image of another, one she mentally calls an enemy, but who her heart calls something else entirely.<br /><br />This sort of conflict was a delight to absorb. Torn between two men - one she must remain with through legal obligation, another she should despise but cannot. Brave Mrs. Woodiwiss! With an interesting ensemble of clever characters, this page-turner is filled with one bizarre situation after another.<br /><br />It's not hard to admire the heroine, as she comes from the worst type of family situation, yet keeps her head high and strong throughout it all. Her devotion to her hubby is touching, while her attraction to the forbidden fruit undeniable. She's thankfully not the sort where her dashing beauty is spoken of in poetry prose every other page. She IS beautiful (naturally), but this is handled with expert tact not to be, well, tacky from the writer.<br /><br />Christopher Seton is adorably fun, with a witty sense of humor, stylish presence, sweet personality that shines when it should, while not being downplayed as a "girley-man" (Insert giggle here please) The tragic husband aroused pity in me, as well as more than compassion, for beneath the mask and ensemble he's an interesting sort that's enchanting to read about. Swamped with villains, from the family to the town enemies, the young heroines doesn't have much time to relax.<br /><br />The book length is generous, and it does take a bit of time for the heroine to finally become married to her scarred Romeo. In fact, I began to wonder if he would show up at all, or if the back cover was a misprint. Plenty of time is taken to reveal characterization and beginning spark between Erienne and Christopher. Speeding up the beginning a smudge certainly wouldn't have hurt, and overall the pacing is quick enough. Plenty of punch in the pages as one disaster after another befalls our main character. In short, I never grew bored with pacing, but the book was a leisurely thrill ride rather than an adrenaline-rushed race. Woodiwiss' writing style was smooth and flowing, enriched with realistic and at times comical dialogue, spruced further along by characters that were anything but three-dimensional shadows.<br /><br />Us readers of romance enjoy a steamy scene time and again; this book doesn't disappoint. There's plenty of built-up sexual tension, of course, particularly in a carriage ride gone erotic. Lovemaking scenes didn't make me see fireworks, but still a delightfully lustrous spark. In scenes of 'trouble', suspense was adequately written with the what's-on-the-line situation being dire. Everything was handled in a realistic, happy go lucky fashion, nothing too far-fetched or silly. The only other troubling aspect is I guessed the ending and turned out right, but oh well, I can't blame Woodiwiss much for my psychic abilities.<br /><br />Thankfully not a trivial book, A Rose in Winter left me grinning more than groaning. Characters embraced me from the start, emitting fierce passion. Pacing worked, although not as well as it could have, the writing style was painlessly addictive, and the end left the characters I had come to care about doing well. Another case of happily ever after, a fairy tale worth reading.<br /><br />And remembering.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3709428654892201122" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_158773884" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/158773884" />
    <a title="Elise Wilson" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1499288-elise-wilson"><img alt="Elise Wilson" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1302204202p2/1499288.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/158773884?book_show_action=true">Apr 04, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Elise Wilson" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Elise Wilson" href="/user/show/1499288-elise-wilson">Elise Wilson</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer158773884" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer664882011046458959">This is my first book by Kathleen Woodiwiss, purchased because of the numerous positive reviews. I was not as enthusiastic about the book as most readers -- those who ranked it 4-5 stars. Woodiwiss certainly demonstrates that she is a good writer and the book has an interesting plot. The beauty and the beast theme generally works well, and the author has put her on spin on it, which is creative. It has its share of mystery, romance and humor.<br/><br/>And while she provides vivid descriptions and details,</span>
  <span id="freeText664882011046458959" style="display:none">This is my first book by Kathleen Woodiwiss, purchased because of the numerous positive reviews. I was not as enthusiastic about the book as most readers -- those who ranked it 4-5 stars. Woodiwiss certainly demonstrates that she is a good writer and the book has an interesting plot. The beauty and the beast theme generally works well, and the author has put her on spin on it, which is creative. It has its share of mystery, romance and humor.<br /><br />And while she provides vivid descriptions and details, they often detract from the reading. I found it too descriptive and too detailed. The story simply did not progress at a good reading pace. For example, we know that Erienne is afraid of the "beast", so we don't need scene after scene telling us/the reader this. And we know that Erienne is beautiful, but to exaggerate her beauty resulting in just about every man who looks at her "desires" her (to the point of rape), is unrealistic.<br /><br />Also, Erienne, our heroine, seems a bit selfish. She willing accepts gifts from the beast, but at the same time fears him and rejects his advances. I wish the romance between Christopher and Erienne had been a bit more developed, because I was not sure at what point they fell in love. What was depicted in the book seemed a shallow relationship based upon his being handsome and rich and her being beautiful -- a sort of love at first sight that never progressed into a meaningful relationship.<br /><br />Some reviewers have suggested that Woodiwiss' writing style is fitting for the period in which she penned the book -- 1979/80. Perhaps so. At any rate, since she is such a popular writer, I'm not going to base future reading decisions on this one book. In fact, I have already purchased "Ashes in the Wind", another book that received great reviews. Woodiwiss not doubt has the gift of writing, I just need to find the right story. </span>
  <a data-text-id="664882011046458959" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText9027950837230004325" style="display:none"><i>4 Stars</i><br /><br />Sheesh! I'm finally done with this oh so long, 567 page, but oh so good novel...<br /><br />They just don't write them like this anymore. <br /><br />I took 1 Star away because there was just way to much information at many parts. I do realize I often complain about books not being long enough these days...but there is absolutely a line that a lot of these older authors loved to cross...But of course when you paid $7 for a book, you knew you were going to be entertained at least 4 days (or a month)...<br /><br />Seton and Erienne's story was well thought out, and I really enjoyed reading about their lives and how they found love...There was one detail missed at the end though...Did she ever meet her real father?! Maybe someone can tell me if I just dozed at that part b/c I see no reason why this wasn't brought to a close...What would've been the big deal in another page or two for goodness sake?!<br /><br />Anyways...<br /><br />Woodiwiss is in the same boat with Sutcliffe for me...Either you love the book or you hate it...there can't be (I don't think) an in between opinion.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer6130104448895196346">I'd give this book a 4.5, so I rounded up.<br/><br/>I loved the story/plot. I loved the characters. I loved the suspense of not knowing what was going to happen next.... It was definitely (and obviously) a Beauty-and-the-Beast story, and once I got through about the first 90 or so pages, I really quite enjoyed it!<br/><br/>The only thing that was a bit difficult for me was Kathleen Woodiwiss's writing style. Very..... FLORID.... which I just looked up to make sure I was using the word correctly: "elaborately or exc</span>
  <span id="freeText6130104448895196346" style="display:none">I'd give this book a 4.5, so I rounded up.<br /><br />I loved the story/plot. I loved the characters. I loved the suspense of not knowing what was going to happen next.... It was definitely (and obviously) a Beauty-and-the-Beast story, and once I got through about the first 90 or so pages, I really quite enjoyed it!<br /><br />The only thing that was a bit difficult for me was Kathleen Woodiwiss's writing style. Very..... FLORID.... which I just looked up to make sure I was using the word correctly: "elaborately or excessively ornamented". Yes. Definitely yes to that. Everything was just SO WORDY. Once I got into the story, I didn't notice as MUCH, but still... <br /><br />During one scene, I almost DIED laughing.... Romance authors use many... errr... euphemisms... for male anatomy, but "flaming sword"??? *snorts* OH GOSH, I read it to my husband so he could laugh with me... We had a great time with that one... ;)<br /><br /></span>

<div id="review_256147737" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/256147737" />
    <a title="Ana" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7278411-ana"><img alt="Ana" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528404309p2/7278411.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/256147737?book_show_action=true">Jan 04, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ana" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ana" href="/user/show/7278411-ana">Ana</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7278411-ana?shelf=lovey-dovey">lovey-dovey</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7278411-ana?shelf=historical-romance">historical-romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer256147737" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3236134229217129807">I really don't understand why I went through with this to the end. It was predictable and boring (most of the time at least) and so freaking cliche that at one point I had a feeling I should just throw the book out the window and be done with it.<br/><br/>Of course, I made the mistake of selecting this book to keep me company on my five hour train ride, and since no one else in the whole bloody compartment had the goodwill to let me borrow one of their books to keep me sane, I simply had to cope with fini</span>
  <span id="freeText3236134229217129807" style="display:none">I really don't understand why I went through with this to the end. It was predictable and boring (most of the time at least) and so freaking cliche that at one point I had a feeling I should just throw the book out the window and be done with it.<br /><br />Of course, I made the mistake of selecting this book to keep me company on my five hour train ride, and since no one else in the whole bloody compartment had the goodwill to let me borrow one of their books to keep me sane, I simply had to cope with finishing this.<br /><br />I may sound a bit biased and angry about this, but let me tell you exactly why this is something you probably shouldn't read (unless you're into those sort of predictable, shallow, cliche books, in which case go right ahead!). First of all, the depth of the characters is completely nonexistent. I don't think I've ever read a book that put so much emphasis on physical appearance as "A Rose In Winter". I mean, the heroine, Erienne, was your typical goddess looking lady, who was apparently the only beautiful woman around, because otherwise I can't explain why any man who ever saw her wanted to cop a feel or rape her! I mean seriously? It seems to me like Mrs. Woodiwiss was a bit of a sexist towards men because for god's sake, no matter how beautiful she is, unless she's part Veela I can assure you not every man is going to sexually harass her the moment he sees her! <br /><br />Anyway, the heroine was way too one-dimensional for my liking. Not to mention the fact that she was shallow to the max! Most of her reasons for rejecting husband material were based on looks alone, and of course she couldn't be happy with the hideous man who lavished her with gifts and love, she had to go for the extremely (and apparently only) handsome guy! Can you get more shallow than that?<br /><br />Secondly, the damsel in distress angle is so overdone! And in this case, regardless of the fact that it was already cliche to begin with, she used it at least a dozen times throughout the book! It seemed like every twenty or so pages, Erienne was being sexually harassed by some ugly duckling and she constantly had to be saved! Because obviously, there wasn't room enough in that pretty little head of hers to learn from her first few experiences and stop being alone with men she didn't trust.<br /><br />Now, seriously, if it weren't for Christopher, I swear to god this wouldn't even have gotten a 1 star rating!</span>
  <a data-text-id="3236134229217129807" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_30683194" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/30683194" />
    <a title="Misfit" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1375548-misfit"><img alt="Misfit" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1496595931p2/1375548.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/30683194?book_show_action=true">Aug 20, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Misfit" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Misfit" href="/user/show/1375548-misfit">Misfit</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1375548-misfit?shelf=historical-romance">historical-romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer30683194" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6279281951777249675">Reasonably entertaining (but predictable) Beauty and the Beast Plot. Erienne Fleming's father, the hard drinking and gambling mayor of their northern England town needs to sell her in marriage to the highest bidder to pay off his gambling debts. Handsome Yankee Christopher Seton wants Erienne, but since Christian is the one he owes the greatest debt to, Christian is banned from bidding for her hand. Instead, Erienne's hand is purchased by the mysterious Lord of Saxton who was horribly injured an</span>
  <span id="freeText6279281951777249675" style="display:none">Reasonably entertaining (but predictable) Beauty and the Beast Plot. Erienne Fleming's father, the hard drinking and gambling mayor of their northern England town needs to sell her in marriage to the highest bidder to pay off his gambling debts. Handsome Yankee Christopher Seton wants Erienne, but since Christian is the one he owes the greatest debt to, Christian is banned from bidding for her hand. Instead, Erienne's hand is purchased by the mysterious Lord of Saxton who was horribly injured and scarred for life in a fire. Erienne is as first horrified by her new husband's appearance and fights her growing attraction to Christopher at the same time and thus begins KEW's take on the <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/41424.Beauty_A_Retelling_of_the_Story_of_Beauty_and_the_Beast" title="Beauty A Retelling of the Story of Beauty and the Beast by Robin McKinley" rel="nofollow noopener">Beauty and the Beast</a>. <br /><br />Unfortunately, as much fun as KEW's romances can be to read, this book has some major flaws. The big twist in the plot is pretty easy to figure out -- as other reviewers have noted. In fact, almost everything in the book is pretty easy to figure out. The bad guys were inept and almost cartoonish in their bad deeds. Erienne is supposed to be intelligent and well educated, but her initial reactions to her disfigured husband just don't ring true, Stuart was nothing but kindness itself and a very gentle and loving husband. She was always running off and getting herself into a pickle so that Christopher could rescue her, and I have to agree with the other reviewers in that it got to be just a tad bit over the top that every man in the book was dying to jump her bones. <br /><br />All in all, not the worst in the historical romance genre, but far from the best either and certainly not one of KEW's better efforts (which would be Ashes in the Wind), but well suited for a rainy Sunday afternoon easy on the brain type of fluff. I'm sorely torn between a two and three star rating, so I'm calling it at 2.5 stars rounded it up to three. </span>
  <a data-text-id="6279281951777249675" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

Yet fate keeps throwing her together with the daring, charming Christopher and she finds herself irresistibly drawn to him, more and more attracted with every meeting. And Christopher keeps declaring his love. <div id="review_2554915547" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2554915547" />
    <a title="Irene" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/36459924-irene"><img alt="Irene" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1589091840p2/36459924.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2554915547?book_show_action=true">Oct 09, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Irene" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Irene" href="/user/show/36459924-irene">Irene</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9780060728687" href="/book/show/7064372-a-rose-in-winter">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36459924-irene?shelf=regency-romances-and-bodice-rippers">regency-romances-and-bodice-rippers</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2554915547" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10369627352038954642">A Rose in Winter is a splendid Beauty and the Beast homage that is a classic in its own right. Fairy tale retellings can be hard to pull off, but well-played, Kathleen E. Woodiwiss! Woodiwiss transports the reader to an idyllic setting of medieval-ish England. Eirenne Fleming's loutish father has sold her in marriage to the highest bidder, and it is Lord Saxton, a man physically damaged after being caught in a horrific fire at his manor a few years ago, and now covers himself from head to toe. L</span>
  <span id="freeText10369627352038954642" style="display:none">A Rose in Winter is a splendid Beauty and the Beast homage that is a classic in its own right. Fairy tale retellings can be hard to pull off, but well-played, Kathleen E. Woodiwiss! Woodiwiss transports the reader to an idyllic setting of medieval-ish England. Eirenne Fleming's loutish father has sold her in marriage to the highest bidder, and it is Lord Saxton, a man physically damaged after being caught in a horrific fire at his manor a few years ago, and now covers himself from head to toe. Lord Saxton's troubles are far from over, however, as roaming bandits nip at his heels, and politicians continue to close in around him. There is a Night Rider stirring up trouble with his Robin Hood exploits, and Eirenne's rakish suitor, Christopher Seton, continues to pursue her, as he is Lord Saxton's cousin.<br /><br />I've never met a "hero has to pretend to be another person to the heroine" plot that I've liked, and A Rose In Winter proves to be no exception. What I can say, however, is that it didn't take away from the story because Christopher is a charmingly naughty suitor. For all the gothic atmosphere, A Rose In Winter has levity to it: Eirenne first meets Christopher, under the assumption that he is a suitor when in fact he is a sworn enemy of the family, and it is a hilarious meet-cute. <br /><br />I will definitely be picking up more of Woodweiss's stories in the future!</span>
  <a data-text-id="10369627352038954642" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText14272739426118543031" style="display:none"> Predictable but still good. <br /><br />QUICK SUMMARY<br />This story reminded me of Beauty and the Beast a bit. Erienne Fleming's father is a drinker and a gambler and mayor of a small english town. Badly needing money to pay his gambling debts and tired of trying to get Erienne to marry money he sells her by public auction. Christopher Seton wants her but Erienne's father forbids him to bid because he is the one he owes the money to and Christopher accused him of cheating.     <a title="J.C. Cassels" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6523498-j-c-cassels"><img alt="J.C. Cassels" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1335470879p2/6523498.jpg" /></a>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="J.C. Cassels" class="user" itemprop="url" name="J.C. Cassels" href="/user/show/6523498-j-c-cassels">J.C. Cassels</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer218004738" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11365779032015858825">This book is one of my top five favorite Romances of all time, and brother, I've read a LOT of them. <br/><br/>Beautiful Erienne Fleming is sold on the block to cover her family's debts. The stipulation is that she will be wedded to the man wealthy enough to satisfy the notes being held by charming gambler, Christopher Seton, who wants her for himself.<br/><br/>When Erienne is bought by the masked, crippled Lord Saxton, and properly wedded, she finds herself torn between two men: The vexing Seton, who happens to be</span>
  <span id="freeText11365779032015858825" style="display:none">This book is one of my top five favorite Romances of all time, and brother, I've read a LOT of them. <br /><br />Beautiful Erienne Fleming is sold on the block to cover her family's debts. The stipulation is that she will be wedded to the man wealthy enough to satisfy the notes being held by charming gambler, Christopher Seton, who wants her for himself.<br /><br />When Erienne is bought by the masked, crippled Lord Saxton, and properly wedded, she finds herself torn between two men: The vexing Seton, who happens to be somehow related to the Saxtons despite his Yankee upbringing, and the tender lover her badly scarred humpback of a husband turns out to be.<br /><br />That, in itself, would be a compelling enough story for me, but in typical Woodiwiss fashion, there is swashbuckling adventure and enough mystery to move this book from a simple Historical Romance to a Romance Classic and a must-read for any fan or would-be fan of the genre.<br /><br />Woodiwiss redefined the Historical Romance Genre. The formula followed by today's stars of the genre are only following the pattern set by Woodiwiss.<br /><br />Do I recommend this book? Absolutely. This one earned a place on my bookshelf nearly thirty years ago and it has become an old friend I turn to again and again.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11365779032015858825" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer7928370949527403313">First, it's not a predictable love story- this book had depth. Ignore the comparison to a Disney story, this ain't it! <br/><br/>One bothersome item: my personal preference tends to rise and set around the Historical Fiction genre. therefore, verbiage/tone didn't fit the time period /location wise.   <span id="freeText7928370949527403313" style="display:none">First, it's not a predictable love story- this book had depth. Ignore the comparison to a Disney story, this ain't it! <br /><br />One bothersome item: my personal preference tends to rise and set around the Historical Fiction genre. therefore, verbiage/tone didn't fit the time period /location wise. (try a mix of western slang w/pinch of traditional Regent Euro romance book style)<br />Then again, *shrugs* it was a damn good story. Even if the wording and slang didn’t match the location of the characters. <br /><br />Refreshing that the romance itself was the center of the story but it didn't consume every page with redundant information. The main Characters had rich personalities as did the supporting cast. Another plus, the book didn't waste pages overly describing their clothing and physical appearance like other romance novels I’ve read as of late. <br /><br />Overall The flow was intense at moments with action and intrigue, yet surrounded by passion &amp; romance story uniquely told.</span>
