<div id="review_293134018" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/293134018" />
    <a title="E_bookpushers" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7274938-e-bookpushers"><img alt="E_bookpushers" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1325131247p2/7274938.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/293134018?book_show_action=true">Mar 12, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="E_bookpushers" class="user" itemprop="url" name="E_bookpushers" href="/user/show/7274938-e-bookpushers">E_bookpushers</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/6093617-a-rose-in-winter">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7274938-e-bookpushers?shelf=own-it">own-it</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7274938-e-bookpushers?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7274938-e-bookpushers?shelf=historical">historical</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7274938-e-bookpushers?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7274938-e-bookpushers?shelf=read-in-2012">read-in-2012</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer293134018" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15978319908592748007">Review originally published at: <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='http://thebookpushers.com/2012/03/14/retro-review-a-rose-in-winter-by-kathleen-e-woodiwiss/'>http://thebookpushers.com/2012/03/14/...</a><br/><br/>Ladies and Gentlemen, It is time for another retro romance review. This is one that I read shortly after I discovered The Bride. In fact it was the second adult romance I ever read. I had to be a little more careful when I was reading this one because it wasn’t on the bookcase, it was in a cubby in my parents’ headboard of their bed. This meant one of them, I was sure it was my mother, was reading it. And if you look at the </span>
  <span id="freeText15978319908592748007" style="display:none">Review originally published at: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://thebookpushers.com/2012/03/14/retro-review-a-rose-in-winter-by-kathleen-e-woodiwiss/">http://thebookpushers.com/2012/03/14/...</a><br /><br />Ladies and Gentlemen, It is time for another retro romance review. This is one that I read shortly after I discovered The Bride. In fact it was the second adult romance I ever read. I had to be a little more careful when I was reading this one because it wasn’t on the bookcase, it was in a cubby in my parents’ headboard of their bed. This meant one of them, I was sure it was my mother, was reading it. And if you look at the cover, I wasn’t sure I was ready for them to see me reading something like that. So I could only read it when my mom wasn’t home. My reading was further complicated because I had to ensure it looked exactly the same each time I was forced to pause so I couldn’t use a bookmark. Then I had the fear that before I finished reading the book would disappear. Lucky me I was able to finish because it has become one of my favorites. As a funny sidenote I was talking to my mother about romances the other day and she insists that before I started pushing to her she had only read romances by Julie Garwood so I don’t know if she ever finished it or if she was even the one reading it…<br /><br /><br /><br />Publisher: Avon Books<br />Publish Date: 1982 (Out Now)<br />How I got this book: Borrowed from my mother’s bookshelf, now purchased<br /><br />Debt-ridden Avery Fleming is determined to find a wealthy husband for his beautiful daughter, Erienne, so he can pay off his mountain of debts. Erienne, however, has refused every one of the old men her father has picked for her consideration. When she meets dashing American merchant Christopher Seton, she cannot deny her attraction to him, despite the fact that he wounded her brother, Farrell, in a duel, crippling him for life. However, when Seton asks for Erienne’s hand in marriage, both she and her father refuse him. Instead, Erienne’s father auctions her off to the highest bidder–the mysterious Lord Saxton, a man whose horrifying scars are hidden by a mask and cloak. Erienne comes to know her husband as a kind and gentle man, but when Christopher Seton returns to town, she cannot fight her attraction to him. She finds herself torn between her duty to the man she has wed and the call of her heart.<br />This blurb came from Goodreads.<br /><br />I have continued to read and enjoy Ms Woodiwiss’ books but this is one of a couple that I read often. When I was re-reading for this review I realized that Ms Woodiwiss, while writing in the era of “bodice rippers” took some different tactics. Her heroine was rather strong-willed and intelligent. She didn’t sit around waiting to be rescued but tried to rescue herself and make the best of her situation. She was also extremely loyal. Sometimes I thought she was too loyal but her actions made sense given her character. Even when she was married and her husband, Lord Saxton, had a monstrous appearance, Erienne continued to remain faithful. I do not tend to like infidelity so I loved it when then heroine decided that she was going to consummate her marriage despite her fears of his physical deformities. Yes she was encouraged by the behavior of a certain individual but she made the choice to go to her husband. It would have been so easy for Erienne to take the other route so the small snippet below is just one of the many scenes that I love with her.<br /><br />“Tis Erienne, milord.” She loosed the belt and dropped her robe, then leaned a knee upon the bed. The waiting silence continued, and drawing up her other knee and climbing onto the mattress, she sat back on her heels. Her voice trembled as she spoke her reason for coming. “My lord, I am less afraid of what you are than what I might become I you do not make me your wife in full. ‘Tis my plea that you take me to you so no further questions might be involved in our marriage.”<br /><br />I didn’t fall in love with the hero, Christopher Seton, for quite some time. First I had my doubts as to how he was going to become the hero. Erienne’s father forbade any interaction between the two since he was the person who wounded Farrell and being a loyal daughter Erienne placed all the blame for her current list of very undesirable suitors on him. Then Erienne was auctioned on the block and married to Lord Saxton so her father could pay his outstanding debts, some directly owed to and others bought by the same Christopher Seton. Prior to the marriage auction, Mr. Seton made a habit of not just pursuing Erienne but also rescuing her from events that might not have happened just yet if he hadn’t been involved. I liked him for all of that but then after the marriage when he continued his attempts to seduce Erienne, which is when I decided that he needed some redemption before becoming a worthwhile hero. Lets just say that Ms Woodiwiss was able to make me believe in Mr. Seton as a hero.<br /><br />Ms Woodiwiss didn’t just deal with the romance but she also included murder mysteries, revenge, highwaymen, a mysterious black rider, lecherous lords and ladies, missing tax revenues and tally books, brutal deaths, unlikely heroes, and gorgeous sounding clothes and jewelry. All of this is woven throughout the story of the romance and also provides some of the impetus for the actions of a few key individuals. The blending of the different threads still seems seamless as I re-read it mumble years later. It still provides me with hours of entertainment since this was also written when novels were expected to have a much longer word-count then now. When I finished reading once again I regretted the shift away from large books because the authors could have a romance span months or even years without losing the reader due to skipped scenes. The characters and settings could also be fully developed without cheating one or the other. I never thought that the story suffered due to a shorter word count.<br /><br />A Rose in Winter doesn’t include any of the balls, Almacks, stale lemonade, rakes who are reformed by the heroine that can appear to be overused in today’s historicals. If you haven’t tried Ms Woodiwiss yet and you are looking for something that doesn’t fit the formula I highly recommend this one.<br /><br />I give A Rose in Winter an A.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15978319908592748007" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText3671021644288031686" style="display:none">Classic-oh-so-very-classic historical romance with a non boring heroine and a quite mysterious plot!<br><br><b><u>UPDATE</u>: 09/17/2012</b><br><br>A Rose in Winter is a story full of intrigue, mystery, suspense and romance. <br><br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[<b>Erienne was...</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380391503i/753944.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>But then she met yankee Christopher Seton.</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380391503i/753945.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>...and he set her lust &amp; ire off!</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380391503ra/753946.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>Then she met Lord Saxton...</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380391503ra/753947.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>And married him!</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380391503ra/753948.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>...and he set her <s>lust &amp; ire</s> off!</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380391503ra/753949.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>But beside him there were things she had for granted.</b><br><br><span>[image error]</span><br><br><b>However he told her...</b> <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380391503i/753951.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>...and she...</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380391503ra/753952.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>Until Christopher Seton's presence became too much and she...</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380391503i/753953.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>Then Lord Saxton revealed to be Christoph-...</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380391503ra/753954.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>...and Erienne's father said...</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380391503ra/753955.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>But Lord Cristopher... Saxton sliced all enemies.</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380391503ra/753956.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>And finally, <i>FINALLY</i>, they managed to...<b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380391503ra/753957.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>And...</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380391503ra/753958.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>And...</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380391503i/753959.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>And...</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380391503i/753960.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>And...</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380391503i/753961.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>- <i>THE END</i> -</b><br></b></b> <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>Once upon a time it was the Flemings. After the mother's death, dad Avery started gambling away all their fortune, until they were forced to move to another city due to debts and his dismissal from his previous post. He continued his cheating in gambling and when a yankee called him upon it, dad Avery let son Farrell to duel with said yankee for the family's honor despite him being in the wrong. Losing the duel, most of his right arm's usage and his self-respect, son Farrell began gambling and drinking as well. That left the family with a single option: get daughter and sister Erienne married to a wealthy - preferrably old too - man, who will pay their debts to the yankee, Christopher Seton, off. After holding them back as much as possible, Erienne is being sold in an auction of sorts and the highest bidder, Lord Saxton, via his vessel <i>purchases</i> her hand in marriage.<br><br>Life as Lady Saxton is full of money, beautiful gowns and jewelry, outings and a husband with a most off-putting, horrifying presence. Masked, crippled and scarred, Lord Saxton terrifies Erienne. However, he never asks for anything, giving her time and space at her request. Erienne comes to love the yankee, Christopher Seton, who still tries to conquer her, and her awe-inspiring, mysterious hunsband, Lord Saxton, who woos her with his caring and kind demeanor.<br><br>In the meanwhile, several murders take place in town due to raidings, and a 'night rider' appears, who seems to be the cause of it all. The leads show a connection for all the events that take place: the Saxton family.<br><br>In this tale I admit I admired Erienne, because she carries herself with dignity, spite and spunk no matter the circumstances. Christopher Seton, gentleman, yankee and scoundrel extraordinaire, is a most charming man, winning the reader - and poor Erienne - over from the moment he shows up. It's impossible not to come to like though Lord Saxton as well. His mysterious, quiet yet thundering presence, holds an irresistible and undeniable allure. The respect and blatant love and admiration he shows towards Erienne add to his good points.<br><br>The story starts off simply. The daughter of a soon-to-be-poor family is being sold off to a wealthy man so that their debts will be paid. Slowly though it becomes much more intriguing and dangerous as more people show up with their own motives, ambitions and purposes. Through a series of events, others of higher and others of less importance, the momentum is conserved, simply switching from one focal point to the next. And it all explodes eventually giving a most satisfying conclusion to the story and its' participants. Needless to say that it's not only the plot that develops, but also the characters. From the first to the very last chapter, the reader realizes they've come a long way and are being judged by their own choices and actions.<br><br>If you're acquainted with Kathleen E. Woodiwiss' novels, you'll know that they're historical, old-fashioned romances, full of long, detailed descriptions and old english. The men are possessive brutes, knaves and/or lords. The women are dumb or witty depending on the role each character serves and the chronological boundaries the book is referring to. So, if by any chance you happen to like good, old, classic romance, here's the author and the book for you!</["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ryn" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ryn" href="/user/show/4392763-ryn">Ryn</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4392763-ryn?shelf=couldn-t-get-through">couldn-t-get-through</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer126533259&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer126533259" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12558492696638384123">Another spin-off of a classic Beauty and the Beast story, only the Beast isn't actually a beast at all, but a gloriously handsome, wonderfully nice, loving man. Which sort of defeats the whole idea of Beauty and the Beast. <br/><br/>However, I don't think the author was aiming for that theme anyway; more a theme of 'One can be gloriously handsome AND be wonderfully caring ALL AT ONCE, especially if one has an equally gorgeous and kindhearted love.' <br/><br/>"But, Ryn!" you say. "Stop being so judgemental when you </span>
  <span id="freeText12558492696638384123" style="display:none">Another spin-off of a classic Beauty and the Beast story, only the Beast isn't actually a beast at all, but a gloriously handsome, wonderfully nice, loving man. Which sort of defeats the whole idea of Beauty and the Beast. <br /><br />However, I don't think the author was aiming for that theme anyway; more a theme of 'One can be gloriously handsome AND be wonderfully caring ALL AT ONCE, especially if one has an equally gorgeous and kindhearted love.' <br /><br />"But, Ryn!" you say. "Stop being so judgemental when you didn't even read the whole book, you silly ****!" All I can say is that I tried. I read right up until she got married to the 'beast' and settled into the tumult of wedded bliss to a masked stranger, with a an insistent old boyfriend demanding benefits on the side. <br /><br />I dislked each character in this book, especially the heroine, who was unintelligent and boring, but beautiful and fiesty, if you can imagine. The combination of these traits made her irritating and useless. I disliked the whole plot, which really could have been a good story, if the author had allowed any flaws whatsoever to create a modicum of depth in her characters. I only rated it one star because I couldn't rate it any lower. </span>

          </span>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1068495338" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9455679185471142929">*** 10 stars read ***<br/><br/>If I could give this book 10 stars I definitely would! It was enthralling in every way possible, the storyline, characters, the love, the emotions,the humour, the prose... I simply could not put this novel down and it kept me reading very late into the night. For me, this is a sign of a 5 ++ star read right away! I loved how Kathleen Woodiwiss was able to give us a very unique love story and at the same time weave into it mystery, action, suspense, and humour. All the elemen</span>
  <span id="freeText9455679185471142929" style="display:none">*** 10 stars read ***<br /><br />If I could give this book 10 stars I definitely would! It was enthralling in every way possible, the storyline, characters, the love, the emotions,the humour, the prose... I simply could not put this novel down and it kept me reading very late into the night. For me, this is a sign of a 5 ++ star read right away! I loved how Kathleen Woodiwiss was able to give us a very unique love story and at the same time weave into it mystery, action, suspense, and humour. All the elements that comprise some of the greatest romance novels. The best element about 'A Rose in Winter' is its uniqueness in how the hero assumed two identities to win the heroine's love. It's a very special type of storyline for the courting of the hero and heroine and of how their love flourished. When you come across a storyline that you've never encountered before, it's a sign of a masterpiece!<br /><br />Did anyone else who read this story find Erienne's cheapskate father hilarious?<br /><br />The only other book I'd read by Kathleen Woodiwiss was 'Shanna'. And that was many years ago, but I remember giving it only 3 stars back then. After being captivated by 'A Rose in Winter', I know I'll give 'Shanna' a second chance and Kathleen Woodiwiss's novels won't stay on my to-read shelves for long!</span>
  <a data-text-id="9455679185471142929" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_57481776" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/57481776" />
    <a title="Keri" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2335749-keri"><img alt="Keri" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1373210138p2/2335749.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

<span id="freeTextContainer9240469024133891776">This was Kathleen Woodwiss's Beauty and the Beast book. Erienne's father gave her hand in marriage to the richest lord in the land, Lord Saxon. Rumors abound about him being half beast and half man. As Erienne finds the courage to go fourth with the marriage in order to save her family, she has to let go the secret in her heart where Christopher Seaton, sassy Yankee that he is, had started to make a place for himself. On the other, Erienne finds herself finding herself having feeling for her rav</span>
  <span id="freeText9240469024133891776" style="display:none">This was Kathleen Woodwiss's Beauty and the Beast book. Erienne's father gave her hand in marriage to the richest lord in the land, Lord Saxon. Rumors abound about him being half beast and half man. As Erienne finds the courage to go fourth with the marriage in order to save her family, she has to let go the secret in her heart where Christopher Seaton, sassy Yankee that he is, had started to make a place for himself. On the other, Erienne finds herself finding herself having feeling for her ravaged and deformed husband as well. Is it possible for a woman to love two men so completely? Timeless fairy tale and one of my absolute favs. My 28 year old copy still looks good for a oversize trade paperback. </span>
  <a data-text-id="9240469024133891776" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('XYNTTAUTYI09iaZHKcZIQCchQg7ivPFEeoE0hUIaVlV754osplnMF1rDv+GCKgkbJKSocN1Zs+gKgp9T78P8Ng==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('Uvj7JfH4F7TQ4yfNGpKIkUSwtIZ2WECXmqG2O7sC9q90nCJFUrK7LrepPmuxfsnKRzVe+Em9Ajvqoh3tFttczA==')})
  }

      <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/88445.Kathleen_E_Woodiwiss">About Kathleen E. Woodiwiss</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/88445.Kathleen_E_Woodiwiss"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1237691529p3/88445.jpg);'></div>
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/88445.Kathleen_E_Woodiwiss">Kathleen E. Woodiwiss
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__followerCount'>
1,450
followers
</div>

</div>
</div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer5334761610224935035">Kathleen Erin Hogg was born on June 3, 1939, in Alexandria, Louisiana, she was the youngest of eight siblings by Gladys (Coker) and Charles Wingrove Hogg, a disabled World War I veteran. She long relished creating original narratives, and by age 6 was telling herself stories at night to help herself fall asleep. At age 16, she met U.S. Air Force Second Lieutenant Ross Eugene Woodiwiss at a dance, </span>
  <span id="freeText5334761610224935035" style="display:none">Kathleen Erin Hogg was born on June 3, 1939, in Alexandria, Louisiana, she was the youngest of eight siblings by Gladys (Coker) and Charles Wingrove Hogg, a disabled World War I veteran. She long relished creating original narratives, and by age 6 was telling herself stories at night to help herself fall asleep. At age 16, she met U.S. Air Force Second Lieutenant Ross Eugene Woodiwiss at a dance, and they married the following year. She wrote her first book in longhand while living at a military outpost in Japan.<br /><br />She is credited with the invention of the modern historical romance novel: In 1972 she released The Flame and the Flower, an instant New York Times bestseller that created a literary precedent. The novel revolutionized mainstream publishing, featuring an epic historical romance with a strong heroine and impassioned sex scenes. The Flame and the Flower was rejected by agents and hardcover publishers, who deemed it as "too long" at 600 pages. Rather than follow the advice of the rejection letters and rewrite the novel, she instead submitted it to paperback publishers. The first publisher on her list, Avon, quickly purchased the novel and arranged an initial 500,000 print run. The novel sold over 2.3 million copies in its first four years of publication.<br /><br />The success of The Flame and the Flower prompted a new style of writing romance, concentrating primarily on historical fiction tracking the monogamous relationship between a helpless heroines and the hero who rescued her, even if he had been the one to place her in danger. The romance novels which followed in her example featured longer plots, more controversial situations and characters, and more intimate and steamy sex scenes.<br /><br />She was an avid horse rider who at one time lived in a large home on 55 acres (220,000 m2) in Minnesota. After her husband's death in 1996, she moved back to Louisiana. She died in a hospital on July 6, 2007 in Princeton, Minnesota, aged 68, from cancer. She was survived by two sons, Sean and Heath, their wives, and numerous grandchildren. Her third son, Dorren, predeceased her.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="5334761610224935035" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
